# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

permissions through middleware, and manage folder/dashboard inheritance. Here are the key architectural components:\\n\\n**Role Definitions (Tier 1):**\\nThe three-tier organization roles are defined in `pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go` as a RoleType enum with four values: RoleNone, RoleViewer, RoleEditor, and RoleAdmin. Each role has a defined precedence order (None=10, Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40) used for permission inheritance. These constants are re-exported in `pkg/services/org/model.go` for use throughout the codebase.\\n\\n**Role-to-Permission Mapping (Tier 2):**\\nThe mapping between organization roles and specific RBAC permissions is built in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` through the `BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()` function, which creates basic role definitions (basic:viewer, basic:editor, basic:admin) with empty permission lists that are later populated. Specific dashboard and folder roles are registered in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` and `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` through `registerDashboardRoles()` and `registerFolderRoles()` functions, which define:\\n- DashboardViewActions (read dashboards, read annotations)\\n- DashboardEditActions (view + write dashboards, delete dashboards, manage annotations)\\n- DashboardAdminActions (edit + read/write permissions)\\n- FolderViewActions (read folders, read alerts, read library panels)\\n- FolderEditActions (view + write folders, create dashboards, create/manage alerts)\\n- FolderAdminActions (edit + read/write folder permissions)\\n\\nThese are registered via `accesscontrol.RoleRegistration` with Grants to the appropriate org roles. The actual permissions are stored in the database and seeded by `pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/basic_role_db_seed.go` through the `refreshBasicRolePermissionsInDB()` function.\\n\\n**Permission Guard Middleware (Tier 3):**\\nPermission enforcement occurs through middleware defined in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go`. The `Middleware()` function wraps HTTP handlers with an `Evaluator`, and the `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()` function creates organization-scoped authorization gates. Both use the `authorize()` function which evaluates permissions against a user's claims via the AccessControl service's `Evaluate()` method, comparing against scoped RBAC permissions (actions with resource scopes like \\\"dashboards:uid:abc123\\\").\\n\\n**Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance:**\\nFolder and dashboard permissions are managed by `pkg/services/accesscontrol/resourcepermissions/service.go`, which provides a generic `Service` with `GetPermissions()` and `SetPermissions()` methods. Inheritance is handled through the `InheritedScopesSolver` callback, which is implemented in `pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go` via the `GetInheritedScopes()` function. This function retrieves parent folder UIDs using `folderService.GetParents()` and generates inherited scopes (e.g., folder:uid:parent1, folder:uid:parent2) so that a user's folder-level permissions cascade to nested dashboards and subfolders.\\n\\nDashboard-specific inherited scopes are resolved through `NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewDashboardIDScopeResolver()` in the same file, which include both the dashboard scope and its parent folder scope hierarchy. When a dashboard is accessed, the permission check includes scopes for the dashboard, its containing folder, and all ancestor folders up the tree, enabling permission inheritance from parent folders.\\n\\n**HTTP API and Service Integration:**\\nThe HTTP API for managing permissions is exposed in `pkg/api/accesscontrol.go` (which declares fixed roles), `pkg/api/dashboard.go`, and `pkg/api/folder.go` (which handle permission checks on API endpoints). The dashboard service in `pkg/services/dashboards/service/dashboard_service.go` uses the `getPermissionsService()` method to route permission operations to either `folderPermissions` or `dashboardPermissions` service instances registered from the OSS access control implementations.\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure:**\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/models.go`: Defines Permission, RoleDTO, and related data structures\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/authorizer.go`: Implements the Authorize interface for permission evaluation\\n- `pkg/services/sqlstore/permissions/dashboard.go`: Implements permission filtering in SQL queries for dashboard access control\\n- `pkg/registry/apis/folders/folder_storage.go`: Sets default folder permissions on creation\\n- `pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder.go`: Implements folder-level permission checks including inherited permissions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that the three-tier permission model is consistently enforced across all dashboard and folder operations, with permissions inherited from parent folders and mediated through RBAC action/scope evaluation.\"\n}\n",

permissions through middleware, and manage folder/dashboard inheritance. Here are the key architectural components:\\n\\n**Role Definitions (Tier 1):**\\nThe three-tier organization roles are defined in `pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go` as a RoleType enum with four values: RoleNone, RoleViewer, RoleEditor, and RoleAdmin. Each role has a defined precedence order (None=10, Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40) used for permission inheritance. These constants are re-exported in `pkg/services/org/model.go` for use throughout the codebase.\\n\\n**Role-to-Permission Mapping (Tier 2):**\\nThe mapping between organization roles and specific RBAC permissions is built in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` through the `BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()` function, which creates basic role definitions (basic:viewer, basic:editor, basic:admin) with empty permission lists that are later populated. Specific dashboard and folder roles are registered in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` and `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` through `registerDashboardRoles()` and `registerFolderRoles()` functions, which define:\\n- DashboardViewActions (read dashboards, read annotations)\\n- DashboardEditActions (view + write dashboards, delete dashboards, manage annotations)\\n- DashboardAdminActions (edit + read/write permissions)\\n- FolderViewActions (read folders, read alerts, read library panels)\\n- FolderEditActions (view + write folders, create dashboards, create/manage alerts)\\n- FolderAdminActions (edit + read/write folder permissions)\\n\\nThese are registered via `accesscontrol.RoleRegistration` with Grants to the appropriate org roles. The actual permissions are stored in the database and seeded by `pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/basic_role_db_seed.go` through the `refreshBasicRolePermissionsInDB()` function.\\n\\n**Permission Guard Middleware (Tier 3):**\\nPermission enforcement occurs through middleware defined in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go`. The `Middleware()` function wraps HTTP handlers with an `Evaluator`, and the `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()` function creates organization-scoped authorization gates. Both use the `authorize()` function which evaluates permissions against a user's claims via the AccessControl service's `Evaluate()` method, comparing against scoped RBAC permissions (actions with resource scopes like \\\"dashboards:uid:abc123\\\").\\n\\n**Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance:**\\nFolder and dashboard permissions are managed by `pkg/services/accesscontrol/resourcepermissions/service.go`, which provides a generic `Service` with `GetPermissions()` and `SetPermissions()` methods. Inheritance is handled through the `InheritedScopesSolver` callback, which is implemented in `pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go` via the `GetInheritedScopes()` function. This function retrieves parent folder UIDs using `folderService.GetParents()` and generates inherited scopes (e.g., folder:uid:parent1, folder:uid:parent2) so that a user's folder-level permissions cascade to nested dashboards and subfolders.\\n\\nDashboard-specific inherited scopes are resolved through `NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewDashboardIDScopeResolver()` in the same file, which include both the dashboard scope and its parent folder scope hierarchy. When a dashboard is accessed, the permission check includes scopes for the dashboard, its containing folder, and all ancestor folders up the tree, enabling permission inheritance from parent folders.\\n\\n**HTTP API and Service Integration:**\\nThe HTTP API for managing permissions is exposed in `pkg/api/accesscontrol.go` (which declares fixed roles), `pkg/api/dashboard.go`, and `pkg/api/folder.go` (which handle permission checks on API endpoints). The dashboard service in `pkg/services/dashboards/service/dashboard_service.go` uses the `getPermissionsService()` method to route permission operations to either `folderPermissions` or `dashboardPermissions` service instances registered from the OSS access control implementations.\\n\\n**Supporting Infrastructure:**\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/models.go`: Defines Permission, RoleDTO, and related data structures\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/authorizer.go`: Implements the Authorize interface for permission evaluation\\n- `pkg/services/sqlstore/permissions/dashboard.go`: Implements permission filtering in SQL queries for dashboard access control\\n- `pkg/registry/apis/folders/folder_storage.go`: Sets default folder permissions on creation\\n- `pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder.go`: Implements folder-level permission checks including inherited permissions\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that the three-tier permission model is consistently enforced across all dashboard and folder operations, with permissions inherited from parent folders and mediated through RBAC action/scope evaluation.\"\n}\n",
